# Backy page and backend completeness audit

Date: 2026-05-10

This audit tracks whether each Backy admin/public surface has the necessary backend and editor behavior expected from a WordPress/Wix/Canva-like product. It is intentionally strict: a page is not complete until it persists through backend APIs, exposes the right public/admin contract, handles loading/empty/error states, and supports the workflows users expect from a production CMS/editor.

## Completion legend

- **Ready**: backend-backed, validated, user-facing behavior is complete for the current product scope.
- **Partial**: usable path exists, but important backend/product behavior is missing.
- **Prototype**: mostly local/mock UI or incomplete workflow.
- **Missing**: route or workflow is absent.

## Product-level gates

Backy should not be called complete until these gates are satisfied:

- **Durable backend**: sites, pages, posts, users, settings, media, forms, comments, events, and publish state are stored in the same durable backend, not split between seed data, localStorage, and local JSON files.
- **Admin APIs**: every admin page has authenticated CRUD endpoints with validation, pagination, RBAC, audit trails, and consistent `{ success, requestId, data/error }` envelopes.
- **Public render contract**: custom frontends can fetch exact site/page/post data, theme tokens, assets, actions, bindings, SEO, and editable maps without relying on admin implementation details.
- **Editor parity**: page/post editing covers Canva/Wix expectations: drag/resize, selection, layers, snapping/alignment, grouping, undo/redo, responsive breakpoints, media/font insertion, template sections, preview, publish, and revision history.
- **Interactive component platform**: pages/posts/blog articles can author trusted interactive blocks, custom figures, code-driven animations, simulations, and fully custom code components through a registry or sandboxed iframe runtime with CSP, permission scopes, versioning, allowed data bindings, fallback render states, and public API contracts. Free-form script boxes are not acceptable for production.
- **WordPress parity**: pages/posts/media/users/settings support drafts, publish/schedule, slugs/permalinks, SEO, revisions, categories/tags where relevant, comments/moderation, forms, roles, and export/import hooks.
- **Operational readiness**: auth, permissions, rate limits, storage quotas, telemetry, backups, webhook retries, tests, and deployment configuration are documented and verified.

| `/login`                    | Ready   | `apps/public/src/app/api/admin/auth/login/route.ts`, `/session`, `/logout`, `/password-recovery`, `/accept-invite`, and `/reset-password` now provide backend-backed admin authentication. Login first attempts configured Supabase Auth password verification from `BACKY_SUPABASE_URL`/`BACKY_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` or aliases, maps the verified email to an existing active Backy admin user, and issues a Backy `authMode: "supabase"` admin session without enabling local demo auth in production; local-demo credentials remain available only when the production local-auth policy allows them. When Settings enables `auth.requireTwoFactor`, successful primary auth now requires a configured `BACKY_ADMIN_MFA_CODE`/`BACKY_ADMIN_2FA_CODE` static verifier or `BACKY_ADMIN_MFA_TOTP_SECRET`/`BACKY_ADMIN_2FA_TOTP_SECRET` TOTP secret before issuing the Backy session, and `/login` reveals a one-time-code field after the API returns `MFA_REQUIRED`; rejected MFA attempts revoke the tentative server session before returning. Successful login, invite acceptance, password reset acceptance, and session refresh now set a `backy_admin_session` httpOnly/SameSite=Lax cookie; session validation, admin access checks, session listing current-session detection, current-session token rotation, and logout accept the cookie while preserving bearer-token compatibility, and logout clears the cookie. Login success, MFA-required, MFA-invalid, MFA-provider-missing, logout, admin-session-rotate, and admin-session-revoke actions now record queryable `auth.*` admin audit events against the Settings security surface, and the Settings audit trail renders readable auth event titles/descriptions plus an auth/API-key/settings filter, summary counts, and detail payload drawer. The Settings security tab can rotate the current browser session, revoke the previous token, refresh the cookie-backed client session, and show the rotation in the auth audit trail; the user detail page lists active admin sessions with current-session protection, last-seen/issued/expires timestamps, and revocation controls. User detail now also exposes a permission-gated per-user MFA panel backed by `GET/PATCH /api/admin/users/:userId/mfa`, persists enrollment and hashed one-time recovery codes in Settings auth metadata, records `user.mfa.update` and `user.mfa.recovery_codes.rotate` audit events, and lets `/api/admin/auth/login` satisfy a user-specific MFA challenge by consuming exactly one recovery code. `apps/admin/src/stores/authStore.ts` signs in through the admin auth API, accepts invite tokens, resets local-demo passwords, persists only user plus session metadata without a readable token, validates and rotates sessions through the httpOnly cookie, scrubs old persisted tokens on rehydrate, and revokes the session on logout. `apps/admin/src/lib/adminAuthApi.ts`, `apps/admin/src/lib/adminContentApi.ts`, and `apps/admin/src/lib/mediaApi.ts` now issue credentialed cookie-first admin requests without reading the session token from localStorage, while `apps/public/src/proxy.ts` allows credentialed CORS for the admin origins. Non-auth admin mutation routes are guarded by server-side `requireAdminAccess` checks, and `npm run test:admin-rbac-coverage --workspace @backy/public` statically verifies every non-auth mutating admin API route calls the access gate, currently covering 92 route files and 116 mutating handlers while excluding only auth lifecycle endpoints that authenticate through invite/reset/session/login tokens; it also source-checks the workspace Settings permission split and the site-scoped Settings `sites.view`/`sites.configure` contract. Login, password recovery, and password reset now share hashed auth rate-limit buckets persisted under Settings auth metadata with separate principal/client limits and retry-after responses; successful login clears prior failed-login counters for that email/client, and password recovery returns a neutral public delivery envelope for known and unknown accounts. The login page now requests password recovery through the backend auth API instead of checking local hard-coded users in the browser, queues password-reset email through Backy's shared transactional provider stack with provider/status metadata while keeping account lookup responses neutral, `/accept-invite?token=...` is a public route that activates pending invited users and starts a session, and `/reset-password?token=...` lets admins set a new local-demo password from a generated reset token. `npm run test:login --workspace @backy-cms/admin` covers invalid credentials, API-backed local recovery with queued reset delivery metadata, successful sign-in, httpOnly cookie issuance, cookie-only session validation, cookie logout/revocation, auth audit readback for login/logout, tokenless persisted session metadata, and dashboard redirect. `npm run test:admin-auth --workspace @backy/public` covers admin-key acceptance/rejection, owner-only key denial, repeated invalid-login rate limiting, neutral known/unknown password-recovery responses, recovery rate limiting, reset password policy, email-domain policy, and invite-only policy. `npm run test:admin-auth-supabase --workspace @backy/public` covers Supabase Auth credential exchange configuration, invalid credential rejection, and provider-unavailable errors; `npm run test:admin-auth-supabase-route --workspace @backy/public` starts a mocked Supabase Auth service plus a temporary public Next server and verifies `/api/admin/auth/login` maps Supabase-verified `admin@backy.io` credentials into an httpOnly-cookie Backy `authMode: "supabase"` session only after missing and invalid MFA codes are rejected without leaving active sessions. `npm run test:settings --workspace @backy-cms/admin` covers the now-enabled Settings two-factor toggle, persisted `auth.requireTwoFactor`, current-session rotation, previous-token rejection, auth audit filtering, and auth audit detail payload rendering. `npm run test:users --workspace @backy-cms/admin` now covers generated invite-link acceptance, user activation, returned session, generated reset-link acceptance, new-password login, active local-demo session history, protected current-session rendering, per-user MFA enablement, one-time recovery-code generation/copy, MFA-required login rejection, recovery-code login success, recovery-code reuse rejection, consumed-code count readback, and `user.invite.accept`/`user.password_reset.accept`/`user.mfa.update`/`user.mfa.recovery_codes.rotate` audit logging. Root admin site list, detail, create, update, and delete routes now apply team-scoped authorization on top of role/permission checks: non-owner sessions only see team-owned sites when they are members, and create/update/delete require owner/admin membership in the target team while admin API keys remain service-level bypasses. `requireAdminAccess` now also resolves `/api/admin/sites/:siteId/...` requests and enforces the same team-owned site gate centrally for nested pages, blog, media, collections, commerce, forms, comments, SEO, navigation, redirects, reusable sections, and frontend-design routes before route handlers run. `npm run test:admin-site-scope --workspace @backy/public` creates a temporary team-owned site plus non-member admin session and verifies list filtering, detail/update `FORBIDDEN_SITE_SCOPE` denial, nested pages list/create denial, and representative nested media, collections, forms, navigation, frontend-design, blog, SEO, redirects, reusable-sections, interactive-components, readiness, duplicate, settings, and commerce denials before cleanup. `npm run test:admin-site-scope:repository --workspace @backy/public` injects database-mode repositories into the real `requireAdminAccess` path and verifies non-member denial, viewer read-only allowance, viewer content-write denial, and editor content-write allowance for nested site routes by id and slug. | `/` dashboard               | Ready   | `apps/admin/src/routes/index.tsx` now loads sites, pages, blog posts, users, media, runtime storage/database/Supabase/Vercel settings, site readiness, recent admin audit logs, and commerce product/order record counts from backend APIs, with local fallback state if the admin API fails and user-directory access degrades independently if that protected endpoint is unavailable. It shows refresh/loading/fallback states, backend health, publishing blockers/warnings, quick creation paths, launch-ready workflow links, module map, API handoff, custom frontend setup links, request-id-backed activity, a launch onboarding checklist with setup progress and next-action links, an operations signal board for commerce catalog/orders, comment/form moderation, and workflow failure/readiness alerts, aggregate analytics for publishing mix, recent audit velocity, lead/comment pressure, and commerce totals, a dashboard-run infrastructure diagnostic panel that reuses the Settings validator for database, media storage, Supabase, and Vercel readiness, and a deployment preflight execution/history panel that records session runs with target URL, request id, and ready/warning/blocked counts. Dashboard data loading and rendered actions are filtered by the signed-in admin permission matrix or role defaults, including privileged users/settings/activity/admin-endpoint surfaces and settings-backed infrastructure/deployment checks. The dashboard design now follows `DESIGN.md` with semantic status tokens and a denser control-room layout. `npm run test:dashboard --workspace @backy-cms/admin` now covers API-backed temporary site creation using a real local-demo admin session, rendered command center/site selector/stats/onboarding/RBAC-scope/deployment-history/operations-signal/aggregate-analytics/readiness/infrastructure diagnostics/workflows/attention/activity/API/module regions, active API site switching with scoped endpoint text, critical builder/navigation links, deployment preflight execution/history rendering, infrastructure check execution, refresh behavior, desktop and mobile rendered visual regression checks for region geometry/control sizing/overflow/runtime overlays, and a temporary viewer-session RBAC pass that verifies users/settings/admin endpoints, privileged creation actions, privileged module cards, and settings-backed checks are hidden or disabled. | `/sites`                    | Ready   | `apps/admin/src/routes/sites.tsx` now loads and deletes through `GET/DELETE /api/admin/sites`, with local fallback state. The multi-site workspace includes command/readiness/RBAC/API/domain-verification/Vercel-deployment/billing-quota/feature-contract/audit/library regions, search plus status/domain/page-coverage filters, CSV/frontend-contract export, per-site publish status editing, selected-site DNS TXT/CNAME verification state, selected-site Vercel preview/production/rollback deployment handoff state, selected-site billing plan and quota usage state, duplicate-as-draft, quick archive, preview/manage links, and typed delete confirmation. The page loads the signed-in user's permission matrix and gates site creation, status/configuration, domain verification, deployment workflow actions, billing/quota changes, duplicate, archive/delete, CSV export, and audit activity visibility by `sites.*`, `settings.billing`, and `activity.export` capabilities. Site create/update/delete APIs now emit queryable `site.created`, `site.updated`, and `site.deleted` admin audit events, and the Sites page renders a request-id-backed Site audit trail panel. Site creation and site duplication now enforce the Settings Commerce billing site limit when overage mode is `block`, returning `BILLING_SITE_LIMIT` before persistence once the workspace reaches the configured site count. `npm run test:sites --workspace @backy-cms/admin` creates a temporary owner and viewer account, temporarily sets Settings billing to block at the current site count and verifies `POST /api/admin/sites` and `POST /api/admin/sites/:siteId/duplicate` reject over-limit creation without persisting a site, creates a temporary site after restoring billing settings, verifies the rendered multi-site command/RBAC/API/domain-verification/Vercel-deployment/billing-quota/feature-contract/audit/library surfaces, persists pending and verified domain verification state through the admin site API, persists Vercel preview queued, preview ready, and production ready deployment state plus run history through the admin site API, persists billing plan changes and quota usage snapshots through the admin site API, publishes it through the status control, exercises search/domain/page/status filters, duplicates it as a draft without carrying the custom domain, archives the original, verifies each mutation and site audit events through the admin API, verifies the viewer session cannot create/configure/verify domains/run deploy workflow actions/change billing quotas/duplicate/archive/delete or view audit activity from the rendered Sites UI, confirms typed deletion as owner, checks layout overflow, captures a screenshot, and cleans up. `npm run test:repositories --workspace @backy/db` now verifies repository-mode site settings JSON persists and reads back domain verification, Vercel deployment history, and billing quota state through the DB site repository and backing DB row. A fresh `/sites` readiness audit reran both suites successfully after the domain, deploy, billing, RBAC, audit, and DB persistence slices landed. | Custom domain billing quota | Ready   | `PATCH /api/admin/sites/:siteId` now enforces the selected site's `settings.billingQuota.limits.customDomains` whenever a custom domain, domain verification domain, or Vercel production domain is changed while Settings Commerce overage mode is `block`. The API returns `BILLING_CUSTOM_DOMAIN_LIMIT` before persistence if the configured domain count would exceed the site quota. `npm run test:sites --workspace @backy-cms/admin` temporarily sets a source site to zero allowed custom domains, verifies a blocked `customDomain` patch returns `BILLING_CUSTOM_DOMAIN_LIMIT`, confirms the blocked domain is not persisted, then restores workspace and site settings. Canvas elements also support shift/command/control-click multi-select from the design surface for grouping and layer operations. The component library now supports composed nested presets and includes hero, feature-grid, lead-capture form, HTML, and table blocks that remain normal editable canvas trees/elements after drop. The editor library also loads active API-backed reusable sections for the active site, can save the selected element tree as a reusable section, can rename/delete saved sections, can insert saved sections as synced canvas instances with source metadata, can refresh a selected synced instance from the saved source, can detach it into an independent editable copy, and still stores concrete canvas trees for public rendering. | `/products`                 | Partial | `apps/admin/src/routes/products.tsx` now exposes a backend-backed commerce catalog workspace for the active site: product schema setup/sync, public-read catalog permissions, readiness checks, public storefront/API handoff manifest, CSV export/import/template controls, filters, product CRUD, variants, option-matrix generation, pricing, inventory policy, delivery URL, checkout URL, subscription enabled/interval/trial metadata, gallery/media fields, category/tags/vendor merchandising, SEO title, publish status, and product editor state. Collection record CSV import now preserves typed number, boolean, tags/multi-reference, and JSON field values so imported catalog data is usable by storefront APIs in demo and database-backed modes, including subscription metadata. Public catalog responses now include a non-secret commerce storefront contract derived from Settings so frontends can read catalog/order-intake availability, default currency, payment-provider handoff mode, provider test/live mode, checkout redirect paths, tax/shipping/discount flags, configurable tax/shipping/discount quote rules, inventory reservation settings, webhook endpoint readiness, webhook event allowlist, and reconciliation mode/window without using admin APIs or leaking webhook secret references; product payloads now also expose a normalized `subscription` object for storefront recurring-plan UI. Products renders a four-variant storefront page-template library that opens `/pages/new` with the products collection id and `datasetMode=list-or-item`for catalog grid, featured collection, product detail, and product launch pages; each template brief includes route model, section expectations, dataset bindings, public commerce APIs, and dynamic-route promotion metadata. Public order intake now validates whole-number item quantities before pricing/reservation, calculates a checkout quote from the product tax class, shipping profile/weight, product discount code, and Settings tax/shipping/discount toggles/rules, calls configured HTTP tax/shipping/discount quote providers during public checkout, applies successful provider adjustments to persisted subtotal/discount/shipping/tax/total fields while surfacing provider adjustment metadata, returns a manual/provider-ready checkout-session handoff when no server Stripe credential is configured, executes Stripe Checkout Session creation when Settings selects Stripe and`BACKY_STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`/`STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`is configured, switches all-subscription carts to Stripe subscription mode with recurring interval and trial-day price data, then persists subtotal, discount, shipping, tax, total, checkout session, payment provider/reference, and customer linkage on the private order record while upserting a private customer profile. Product records also expose a provider catalog sync action:`POST /api/admin/sites/:siteId/commerce/products/:productId/provider-sync`validates`commerce.edit`, stores safe `providersync`metadata, records a`commerce.product.provider_sync`audit event, falls back to handoff metadata when execution config is absent, creates Stripe Product/Price records through the configured Stripe API when`BACKY_STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`/`STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`is available, creates PayPal catalog products plus PayPal subscription billing plans when`BACKY_PAYPAL_ACCESS_TOKEN`/`PAYPAL_ACCESS_TOKEN`or PayPal client credentials are available, creates Paddle Product/Price records through the configured Paddle API when`BACKY_PADDLE_API_KEY`/`PADDLE_API_KEY`is available, upserts a Square Catalog Item/Variation through the configured Square API when`BACKY_SQUARE_ACCESS_TOKEN`/`SQUARE_ACCESS_TOKEN`is available, creates Shopify Admin API products/variants with Backy metafields when`BACKY_SHOPIFY_ADMIN_ACCESS_TOKEN`/`SHOPIFY_ADMIN_ACCESS_TOKEN`plus store domain or Admin API base URL are available, creates BigCommerce Catalog API products/variants with Backy custom fields when`BACKY_BIGCOMMERCE_ACCESS_TOKEN`/`BIGCOMMERCE_ACCESS_TOKEN`plus store hash or API base URL are available, creates WooCommerce REST API products and variations when`BACKY_WOOCOMMERCE_CONSUMER_KEY`/`WOOCOMMERCE_CONSUMER_KEY`, `BACKY_WOOCOMMERCE_CONSUMER_SECRET`/`WOOCOMMERCE_CONSUMER_SECRET`, and store URL or API base URL are available, creates Etsy draft listings when`BACKY_ETSY_ACCESS_TOKEN`/`ETSY_ACCESS_TOKEN`, `BACKY_ETSY_API_KEY`/`ETSY_API_KEY`, and `BACKY_ETSY_SHOP_ID`/`ETSY_SHOP_ID` are available, and executes a configured HTTP catalog sync provider from Settings or `BACKY_COMMERCE_PRODUCT_SYNC_URL`with a safe`backy.commerce-product-sync.v1`payload that includes product, variant, delivery, inventory, checkout, and subscription metadata; the Products editor renders the provider sync state and exposes Auto, Stripe, PayPal, Paddle, Square, Shopify, BigCommerce, WooCommerce, Etsy, Magento, and HTTP catalog-sync controls. Product operation endpoints now return Backy contract/cache headers for custom admin clients: provider sync emits`backy.commerce-product-sync.v1`, subscription lifecycle emits `backy.product-subscription-lifecycle.v1`, and lifecycle actions emit `backy.product-subscription-action.v1`, all with private/no-store cache scope. Products also renders a Product API response contracts panel and includes an `apiContracts`block in the exported product handoff manifest, mapping public catalog, order intake, provider sync, subscription lifecycle, subscription action, and product automation event endpoints to schema ids, methods, cache scope, and response headers. Products reads private customer profiles and paid order line items back into the commerce signal panel, ranks product performance by units/revenue/orders with current stock/low-stock context, includes that product-performance signal in the handoff manifest, and includes inline profile-management controls for name, email, phone, lifecycle status, and internal notes using the existing admin collection-record PATCH path. The page exposes usage analytics for the loaded library: storage/type mix, referenced vs unused counts, public/private delivery counts, replacement/version counts, largest assets, and actionable All/Unused/Referenced/Replaced grid focus controls. The media storage panel now shows the active runtime provider, quota, Supabase project/bucket readiness, missing environment fields, a direct Infrastructure settings link, Media-page "Run check" plus "Provision probe" actions that reuse the Settings infrastructure validator for storage/Supabase diagnostics, and a dedicated "Rotation probe" action that validates provider-specific replacement credential environment variables before operators promote them. The provisioning path can create or verify the configured local uploads directory/Supabase Storage bucket/S3-compatible bucket when credentials allow it, and verifies the active bucket/path can upload, read, stat, list, and clean up a probe object. The same storage panel can edit and save media.configure-gated non-secret provider metadata from Media itself: provider, bucket, public base URL, path prefix, private file delivery, image transforms, Supabase project URL/ref, and Supabase storage enablement, while keeping secrets in environment variables. It now also renders a provider-specific environment contract for local, Supabase, and S3-compatible storage, including required env vars, optional vars, secret indicators, and current missing/detected status so operators have the runtime credential checklist beside the Media setup form; provisioning and credential-rotation probes return provider-specific credential fields plus no-secrets promotion runbooks. The media storage surface now also renders upload-scanner runtime status plus a scanner env contract for `BACKY_MEDIA_SCAN_*`, including provider, HTTP endpoint, ClamAV clamd host/port, optional bearer key, timeout, and fail-open semantics, while admin settings exposes the same non-secret `runtimeMediaScanner` summary for custom admin frontends. The media detail dialog exposes delivery controls for custom frontends: public file endpoint URLs, time-limited signed URL generation with expiry/disposition controls, public image transform URL generation for optimized frontend image delivery, prepared responsive image `srcset` manifests with generated WebP byte/provider metadata, Backy-served delivery analytics, static upload safety scan status, stable-ID file replacement, replacement history, and a per-asset activity trail from admin audit logs. Page/post save, rollback, and delete flows sync media usage references, and `POST /api/admin/sites/:siteId/media/:mediaId/bind` can explicitly bind/unbind media to page/post contexts. Public media catalog hides private items, while public font media is exposed through `/render` `assets.fonts` with `weights`, `styles`, `fallbackStack`, `display`, and `cssFamily`; hosted pages/posts inject matching `@font-face` rules. Admin integrations can now mint temporary signed media file URLs through `POST /api/admin/sites/:siteId/media/:mediaId/signed-url`, and `/api/sites/:siteId/media/:mediaId/file` blocks unsigned private files while serving valid signed private bytes from the storage adapter and recording Backy-served request/byte analytics. Public image assets expose a `responsive` manifest in list/detail responses, `POST /api/admin/sites/:siteId/media/:mediaId/transforms` now generates stored WebP variants through the active storage adapter while accounting generated bytes against quota, and `/api/sites/:siteId/media/:mediaId/transform?width=...&quality=...` remains a validated on-demand optimizer fallback that records transform request analytics, with manifest/OpenAPI/SDK exposure and admin smoke coverage. Uploads and replacements enforce a per-site media quota from `BACKY_SITE_MEDIA_QUOTA_BYTES` with a 500 MB default, run static safety checks before storage, can optionally forward bytes to a fail-closed HTTP scan provider or built-in ClamAV `clamd` INSTREAM adapter configured through `BACKY_MEDIA_SCAN_*` env vars, reject active-content SVG or provider-rejected payloads, return quota usage on upload/list/replace responses, and count retained replacement versions plus generated transform bytes against storage usage. The Vercel environment secret-manager path now executes provider-native storage credential promotion/revocation without storing raw secrets in Backy: promotion upserts replacement `BACKY_*_NEXT_*` values into active Vercel project env vars using `upsert=true`, stores secret storage credentials as Vercel sensitive variables, rejects development-target secret promotion, and replacement revocation deletes the NEXT env vars after promotion. `npm run test:media --workspace @backy-cms/admin` now covers API-backed folder creation, public image and private file upload, rendered media command storage/Supabase infrastructure check rendering, Media-page provisioning probe rendering with bucket automation, dedicated credential rotation probe rendering, detail-dialog stable-ID file replacement with retained replacement history, responsive variant preparation with generated transform metadata, metadata editing with visibility changes and API readback, temporary signed URL generation from the details dialog, delete confirmation, layout checks, screenshot capture, and cleanup. `npm run test:media-secret-manager --workspace @backy/public` starts a temporary public app with S3 replacement env vars and a mocked Vercel REST API, verifies authenticated promote/revoke requests hit the configured Vercel API base with bearer auth/team id, asserts active variables are upserted with sensitive secret typing and production/preview targets, asserts raw replacement secrets are not returned, verifies development-target secret promotion is blocked before any provider call, and verifies replacement env revocation deletes every mapped NEXT variable. `npm run test:media-safety --workspace @backy/public` verifies optional scanner hooks across default static scanning, clean HTTP provider verdict metadata, HTTP provider rejection, missing HTTP endpoint fail-closed/fail-open behavior, ClamAV clean verdict metadata, ClamAV infected rejection, ClamAV availability fail-open behavior, and unsupported-provider errors. `npm run test:media-quota --workspace @backy/public` verifies low-quota rejection against a configured server. `@backy/storage` provides local/S3/R2/Supabase adapter contracts for upload/read/delete/sign/list/stat, with local path traversal coverage in `npm run test:smoke --workspace @backy/storage`; public runtime media storage now selects local, S3/R2-compatible, or Supabase storage from environment variables and exposes a non-secret runtime summary through admin settings. Upload/replacement metadata stores the provider storage path and safety scan result so private file reads and deletes do not depend on reverse-parsing remote public URLs. Media create/update/delete, replace, transform preparation, provider analytics ingest, storage provisioning, credential-rotation probe, Vercel secret-manager execution, and explicit bind/unbind now emit queryable admin audit logs with request-id correlation, existing-media mutation routes require media.edit while upload/folder-create require media.create and destructive routes require media.delete, provider/CDN metrics persist request/byte/conversion/value attribution fields, the library analytics panel renders provider ROI totals for attributed value/conversions/CVR/value per request, retained-version comparisons include media-aware preview fallbacks, and `npm run test:repositories --workspace @backy/db` covers DB-backed media version create/list/delete cleanup. | Collection APIs                                        | Ready  | `GET/POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/admin/sites/:siteId/collections` and nested `/records` endpoints support demo persistence and repository persistence through `BackyCollectionRepository`, `packages/db/src/repositories/collections.ts`, and `packages/db/src/schema/index.ts`. | Public hosted pages | Ready | `apps/public/src/app/sites/[subdomain]/[[...path]]/page.tsx` renders page content, supports token-gated draft page previews, resolves collection-bound page element values before rendering, renders generated collection item pages for published `/:collectionSlug/:recordSlug` records, and applies site-level redirect/gone settings before normal page resolution. ## Immediate implementation order

1. **Real admin persistence API**: add authenticated admin endpoints for sites/pages/posts/users/settings and move admin store writes behind API helpers.
2. **Editor completion pass**: layers panel, snapping/alignment, undo/redo hardening, responsive canvas modes, composed presets, saved reusable sections, preview/publish, revision autosave, and conflict-safe save/reload recovery.
3. **Media management completion**: public media feeds now expose cache revision headers/ETags and admin asset details expose queryable activity, replacement history, retained-version compare/restore/deletion with checksum/path/name/timeline diff review and media previews, library usage analytics, generated responsive image manifests, Backy-served delivery counts, manual provider/CDN metric recording with conversions/value attribution, batch provider/CDN metric ingestion, provider ROI rollups, scanner runtime contract, HTTP/ClamAV provider scan behavior, detail/bulk quarantine workflows, bucket creation/verification automation, replacement-credential rotation probes, S3-compatible lifecycle policy automation, and Backy-managed lifecycle cleanup for providers such as Supabase/local where native lifecycle APIs are unavailable; storage secret-reference metadata and readiness checks now prevent raw credential persistence, and broader external cloud secret-manager writeback remains a platform integrations backlog item.
4. **Publishing model**: add cache invalidation, preview token audit events, and broaden hosted preview tests into the main CI path.
5. **Backend validation/test suite**: broaden endpoint contract tests (`test:preview-contract`, `test:admin-contract`), editor serialization tests, render payload schema validation, and smoke tests for every admin page.

## Product backlog notes

- **Reusable admin UI system**: continue moving every page onto shared Backy-owned primitives for buttons, panels, pills, tabs, notices, empty states, tables, and form controls before adding page-local styling.
- **Blog/page editor organization**: the blog editor now uses a shared workspace frame and better grouped toolbar controls, and the shared page editor can persist desktop/tablet/mobile responsive overrides, but the canvas, component rail, layers/properties panels, page size controls, autosave, preview, and post settings still need a deeper organization pass so users can freely design complex pages without the surface feeling cramped or scattered.
- **Interactive animation/code components**: add a first-class `interactiveFigure`/`codeComponent` block family for blogs and pages so authors can build data-driven animations, simulations, calculators, diagrams, custom visualizations, and fully bespoke interactive designs such as self-correction figures, round-based simulations, and scroll/step-controlled blog diagrams. This is a platform feature, not a free-form script box: animation execution is frontend-side, while Backy owns the content model, data bindings, controls, publishing, API contract, registry, and safety boundary. Fully custom code must run through a safer component registry or constrained iframe sandbox with CSP, permissions, versioning, signed/integrity-checked bundles, and allowed data bindings before it can be selected in blog/page content. Implementation checklist:
  1. Done: backend content model for `componentKey`, `version`, `props`, `controls`, `dataBindings`, sizing, fallback content, and render capability metadata.
  2. Done for registry records: safe component registry APIs with ownership, allowed data scopes, dependency metadata, status/review state, rollback, audit events, file-backed demo persistence, and production repository/schema wiring.
  3. Done for runtime shell: sandboxed iframe runtime with strict CSP, sandbox flags, permission allowlists, postMessage protocol, resize/error reporting, and static fallback behavior.
  4. Done for authoring path: editor controls for trusted interactive figures and registered code components, including registry selection, preview, data-source binding, fallback editing, and publish readiness checks.
  5. Done for external contracts: public render payloads, frontend manifest, OpenAPI, and SDK types expose trusted components, iframe sandbox metadata, and sandbox response-header contracts without depending on admin internals.
  6. Done for usage inventory: admin component versions expose a page/blog usage scan before delete, rollback, review, or migration workflows, including target resource, element id/path, render mode, fallback coverage, and scanned counts.
  7. Done for author templates: the editor component library now includes self-correction rounds, step-through diagram, and data-bound line-chart presets backed by registry component keys and required fallback metadata.
  8. Done for import/export metadata: admin component versions export a portable `backy.interactive-component-export.v1` package with runtime, bundle, dependency, import-target, and usage-inventory metadata, and the create API can import that package as a draft component while preserving source metadata.
  9. Done for component-version migration tools: admin component versions expose dry-run/apply migration across draft, scheduled, published, and archived page/blog content, update matching nested component elements to a target key/version, preserve fallback metadata, create revisions, and emit migration audit/cache invalidation metadata.
  10. Done for integrity/dependency verification: custom/sandbox component create/update/review validates runtime URLs, iframe sandbox flags, allowed permissions, signed integrity metadata before approval, dependency names/versions, blocked runtime modules, and lifecycle-script fields.
  11. Done for bundle review/approval workflow: component versions expose an explicit submit/approve/reject review endpoint with server-side validation, disabled draft/in-review states, approval/rejection metadata, audit logs, and cache invalidation.
  12. Done for signed bundle storage: admin component versions can store base64 `.js`, `.mjs`, or `.json` bundles through the configured storage adapter, compute server-side SHA-256, attach caller-provided or registry-HMAC signature metadata, update runtime bundle URLs, preserve sandbox routing, and emit bundle upload audit/cache invalidation metadata without executing uploaded code.
  13. Done for Supabase/Postgres registry smoke coverage: `npm run test:repositories --workspace @backy/db` now exercises the DB-backed interactive component repository through create/list/detail/update/rollback/delete, including approved sandbox runtime metadata, signed integrity hash/signature fields, Supabase-style storage provider/path metadata, and dependency bundle metadata persistence.
  14. Done for hostile-bundle browser security tests: `npm run test:interactive-sandbox-security --workspace @backy/public` statically verifies public/admin interactive iframe allowlists exclude same-origin, top-navigation, and popup-escape flags, verifies server-side validation rejects dangerous sandbox flags and broad permissions, and launches headless Chrome with a hostile sandboxed iframe to prove parent DOM/location/cookies/localStorage, top navigation, and popup escape attempts are blocked.
  15. Done for broader author templates: the editor component library and public registry now include timeline, parameter simulation, data explorer, and sandboxed canvas animation presets with pinned component keys/versions, declared control schemas, data scopes, fallbacks, and Backy-owned sandbox runtime metadata so authors can compose richer research-style interactive figures without inline scripts.
  16. Done for registry policy/binding hardening: public registry entries now expose dependency policy presets, animation-library compatibility metadata, and data-binding preset declarations for trusted figures and sandboxed code components; the editor inspector renders dependency policy, compatibility, and animation-library badges before publish, provides registry-declared binding preset buttons that persist the selected binding target into the canvas element, and the public OpenAPI/SDK contracts describe those fields for custom frontends.
  17. Done for representative animation runtime browser fixture: `npm run test:interactive-sandbox-security --workspace @backy/public` now keeps the hostile-access browser fixture and also mounts a sandboxed canvas animation runtime that receives Backy's `backy.interactive-component.init` payload, echoes component identity, emits ready/resize lifecycle messages, renders multiple frames, and proves changing canvas samples while preserving the same constrained iframe sandbox/referrer policy.
  18. Done for compatibility/version enforcement: server-side interactive component validation now normalizes registry `dependencyPolicy`, `compatibility`, and `dataBindingPresets` into existing dependency metadata, rejects unsafe dependency policy presets, lifecycle scripts, remote runtime policies, unbounded Backy runtime compatibility, render-target mismatches with the selected render mode, missing `static-fallback` compatibility, and malformed binding preset schemas across create/update/review/bundle mutation paths, and public registry discovery maps the persisted metadata back out as first-class contract fields.
  19. Done for richer visual previews: the interactive inspector now renders a compact registry-driven visual preview panel for rounds, stepper, chart, timeline, simulation, data explorer, and sandboxed canvas/custom component families. The preview shows the selected title, render mode, family-specific caption, feature chips, and control-influenced miniature output so authors can identify the selected interactive design before publishing without reading component internals.
  20. Done for sandbox response-header contracts: frontend manifest, public interactive registry, OpenAPI sandbox operation responses, OpenAPI component schemas, generated SDK contract types, and the handwritten SDK manifest type now expose the Backy-owned sandbox CSP, permissions policy, referrer policy, and nosniff guarantees as required contract fields. `npm run test:generated-types --workspace @backy/sdk-js`, `npm run typecheck --workspace @backy/public`, `npm run typecheck --workspace @backy/sdk-js`, and `npm run test:interactive-sandbox-security --workspace @backy/public` verify the contract shape and security source guards, including generated and SDK-convenience negative type cases that reject missing sandbox response-header guarantees.
- **Page editor conflict safety**: page editor saves now send `expectedUpdatedAt`, stale backend PATCH requests return `PAGE_VERSION_CONFLICT`, the editor renders a save-conflict banner with editor/backend timestamps plus a reload-latest action, and `BACKY_EDITOR_CONFLICT_SMOKE=1 npm run test:editor-drag --workspace @backy-cms/admin` verifies a stale save is blocked without overwriting the newer backend copy.

Operators can choose the `BACKY_DATABASE_URL` or `DATABASE_URL` alias, enter optional `BACKY_DATABASE_CERTIFICATION_EXPECTED_HOST` and `BACKY_DATABASE_CERTIFICATION_EXPECTED_DATABASE` target guards, toggle disposable confirmation and the non-secret release doctor, then copy the generated `npm run ci:forms-postgres` command without ever pasting a database URL into Backy metadata. `GET /api/admin/sites/:siteId/forms` exposes the same non-secret `persistenceCertification.operatorCommandTemplate`, and `apps/admin/scripts/forms-smoke.mjs` plus `npm run test:forms-postgres-preflight-contract` source-guard the UI/API strings while the row remains Partial until the command runs against a migrated disposable Supabase/Postgres database.

The standalone Forms/SDK workflows run the non-secret certification doctor plus write the same guard/confirmation evidence to `GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY`, including the exact Partial row and gate (`/forms` -> `npm run ci:forms-postgres`, Frontend manifest/OpenAPI/SDK APIs -> `npm run ci:sdk-postgres-smoke`), aggregate preflight coverage, and the admin source guard without logging database credentials. The runtime evidence covers database, storage, Supabase, Vercel, media scanning, notifications, commerce, interactive components, and public API/CORS readiness without returning provider secrets, so custom admin clients receive the same live-provider certification handoff that the Settings UI exposes while real provider certification remains external. `apps/public/scripts/admin-contract-smoke.mjs` source-guards the route contract and response-tests the provider certification schema, status, gate names, preflight names, runtime evidence, secret-handling guidance, and family coverage.

The handoff names database/Supabase aliases such as `BACKY_DATABASE_URL`/`DATABASE_URL` and `BACKY_SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`/`SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`, storage aliases such as `BACKY_S3_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY`/`AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY`, Vercel aliases such as `VERCEL_PROJECT_ID`/`BACKY_VERCEL_PROJECT_ID`, notification aliases such as `BACKY_EMAIL_DELIVERY_ENDPOINT`/`BACKY_TRANSACTIONAL_EMAIL_WEBHOOK_URL` and `BACKY_RESEND_API_KEY`/`RESEND_API_KEY`, plus commerce aliases such as `BACKY_COMMERCE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`/`COMMERCE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`. `test:settings-admin-contract` now response-tests the returned required-input aliases, and `test:settings-provider-certification-preflight-contract` source-guards the route, response test, and API-contract docs so custom admin clients do not drift behind the credential surface accepted by the manual Settings provider certification workflow.
- **Settings UI provider-alias handoff guard**: the `/settings` handoff manifest and visible provider-certification matrix now use the same `backy.settings-provider-certification-handoff.v1` schema and expanded `providerCertification.groups[].requiredInputs` alias families as `GET /api/admin/settings`, including Supabase, S3, Vercel, notification, Avalara, carrier, and commerce webhook aliases. The visible matrix also renders the schema/status/local-preflight/secret-boundary summary so operators can verify `external-live-provider-gate`, `npm run test:settings-provider-certification-preflight-contract`, and the server/CI-only credential rule before a live provider run. `apps/admin/scripts/settings-smoke.mjs` and `test:settings-provider-certification-preflight-contract` source-guard those UI strings so the admin Settings page cannot show weaker certification instructions than the API contract.
- **Settings release schema handoff guard**: the release certification runbook now documents that `GET /api/admin/settings` and `/settings` expose `providerCertification.schemaVersion = backy.settings-provider-certification-handoff.v1` as the shared non-secret Settings handoff. `test:release-certification-preflight-contract` source-guards that runbook and audit text, so the top-level release checklist cannot drift behind the Settings API/UI schema used by custom admin clients and manual live-provider certification.
- **Settings certification summary update**: the standalone Settings provider certification workflow now writes non-secret `GITHUB_STEP_SUMMARY` evidence for the `/settings` and Settings admin APIs Partial row, optional nested `/products` and `/orders` Commerce Partial row, their `npm run ci:settings-provider-certification` / `npm run ci:commerce-provider-certification` gates, aggregate preflight/admin source guard coverage, local/external Settings and nested-Commerce targets, external admin-key configured booleans, plus selected storage, notification, payment, tax, shipping, discount, catalog, subscription, and webhook provider families, matching the release workflow summary without printing external URLs, admin keys, or provider secrets. The Settings provider runner also rejects required certification runs that select no Settings certification group before starting diagnostics, rejects malformed external target URLs before certification work, and external-target runs now require an explicit `BACKY_ADMIN_API_KEY` or `BACKY_SETTINGS_CERTIFICATION_ADMIN_KEY` instead of using the local generated key path. The standalone Settings and top-level release workflows now forward secret-backed Settings/Commerce certification admin-key aliases instead of generated local keys, so external-target runs fail early when the deployed admin key has not been configured.
- **Settings provider certification handoff**: `/settings` now renders a visible Provider certification matrix in the release-certification runbook and includes the same non-secret `providerCertification` block in the Settings handoff manifest. The matrix separates Settings provider certification from Commerce provider certification, names the live provider families for Supabase/Postgres/Auth/Storage, local/Supabase/S3 media storage and scanner checks, Vercel project/domain/env-secret planning, Webhook/Resend/SMTP/local-outbox notifications, and commerce providers including Stripe, TaxJar, Avalara, EasyPost, Shippo, PayPal, Paddle, Square, Adyen, Mollie, Razorpay, Shopify, BigCommerce, WooCommerce, Etsy, and Magento. `apps/admin/scripts/settings-smoke.mjs` source-guards the rendered matrix, manifest field, gate names, representative provider labels, and secret-alias families so the remaining `/settings` Partial status is tied to explicit live-provider certification evidence instead of only prose release notes.
- **Settings provider runtime evidence panel**: `/settings` now renders the Settings runtime evidence from the provider-certification handoff as visible, non-secret UI under the Provider certification matrix. The panel summarizes database, storage, Supabase, Vercel, notifications, commerce, media scanner, interactive components, and public API/CORS readiness, including missing runtime input aliases without exposing credential values. `apps/admin/scripts/settings-smoke.mjs` and `test:settings-provider-certification-preflight-contract` source-guard the rendered `settings-provider-runtime-evidence` block, runtime readiness count, public API/CORS row, and secret-boundary copy while the Settings rows remain Partial until live provider certification runs.
- **Settings provider certification command builder**: `/settings` now turns the provider-certification matrix into a copyable shell command builder for selected storage, credential-rotation, Vercel-secret, notification, and nested-commerce certification families. The builder emits non-secret `export` lines for `BACKY_SETTINGS_PROVIDER_CERTIFICATION_REQUIRED`, `BACKY_SETTINGS_CERTIFY_STORAGE_PROVIDER`, `BACKY_SETTINGS_CERTIFY_NOTIFICATION_PROVIDER`, optional external-target/admin-key placeholders, and the Settings/Commerce CI commands, plus a selected required-alias list. `GET /api/admin/settings` exposes the same `operatorCommandTemplate` in the non-secret `providerCertification` contract, and `apps/admin/scripts/settings-smoke.mjs` plus `test:settings-admin-contract` source-guard the UI/API strings while the row remains Partial until live provider runs pass.
- **Settings nested Commerce certification parity update**: the standalone Settings provider certification workflow now exposes the same discount and Razorpay subscription selectors as the Commerce certification runner and release workflow, and forwards the full nested Commerce provider env surface for PayPal, Paddle, Square, Adyen, Mollie, Razorpay, Stripe discounts, HTTP discount endpoints, provider webhooks, provider API-base overrides, and catalog API-base/store alternatives before invoking `ci:commerce-provider-certification`. `test:settings-provider-certification-preflight-contract`, `test:commerce-provider-certification-preflight-contract`, and `test:release-certification-preflight-contract` now parse the workflow choice blocks and assert the exact supported storage, notification, payment, tax, shipping, discount, catalog, subscription, and webhook provider option lists, including that `subscription_provider` specifically exposes `razorpay` rather than accepting unrelated Razorpay workflow/env mentions. `test:settings-provider-certification-preflight-contract` also source-guards those forwarded env names so the Settings-owned certification gate cannot silently become weaker than the standalone Commerce gate.
- **Settings notification env contract update**: the Settings infrastructure env contract now surfaces the same notification delivery aliases that the runtime diagnostics, release doctor, and certification workflows accept: `BACKY_EMAIL_DELIVERY_ENDPOINT`/`BACKY_TRANSACTIONAL_EMAIL_WEBHOOK_URL` for HTTP endpoint delivery plus optional `BACKY_SMTP_USER`/`SMTP_USER` and `BACKY_SMTP_PASSWORD`/`SMTP_PASSWORD` rows for authenticated SMTP. `apps/admin/scripts/settings-smoke.mjs` and `test:settings-provider-certification-preflight-contract` guard those rows so operators can configure notification certification from the UI instead of relying on external runbook knowledge.
- **Settings certification database alias update**: the standalone Settings provider certification workflow now forwards `DATABASE_URL` alongside `BACKY_DATABASE_URL`, matching the local runtime and release doctor alias contract when a local Settings certification target needs repository/database mode. `test:settings-provider-certification-preflight-contract` source-guards both env names so the Settings provider gate stays aligned with the Forms, SDK, and release database certification workflows.
- **Settings database alias UI contract update**: `/settings` now surfaces the `BACKY_DATABASE_URL`/`DATABASE_URL` alias family in the release-certification handoff and visible database-gate runbook, and the Settings smoke plus provider-certification preflight guard that both names remain discoverable from the UI before operators run the Forms and SDK Postgres gates.
- **Settings storage alias certification update**: the standalone Settings and release certification workflows now forward runtime-compatible storage aliases beside the Backy-prefixed names, including `BACKY_MEDIA_STORAGE_PROVIDER`, Supabase `SUPABASE_URL`/`SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`, S3 `AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID`/`AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY`/`AWS_REGION`, and next-credential rotation aliases. - **Settings Vercel alias certification update**: the standalone Settings and release certification workflows now forward `BACKY_VERCEL_TOKEN`, `BACKY_VERCEL_PROJECT_ID`, `BACKY_VERCEL_TEAM_ID`, and `VERCEL_API_BASE_URL` beside the existing Vercel names, matching the Settings runtime and release doctor env contract. - **Settings provider certification selector update**: `ci:settings-provider-certification` now accepts `BACKY_SETTINGS_CERTIFY_STORAGE_PROVIDER` with `auto`, `local`, `s3`, or `supabase`, verifies storage provisioning and rotation probe provider output against that selected family, and reports the requested storage provider in certification output. - **Site webhook execution update**: site-level webhook configuration now includes a first-class `site-updated` event kind. `PATCH /api/admin/sites/:siteId` dispatches enabled site webhook endpoints subscribed to `site-updated` after domain, theme/publish, general site, or webhook configuration changes, sends a `backy.site-webhook.v1` payload with site identity, request id, reason, actor, before/after data, and section metadata, applies a bounded delivery timeout, records queued/succeeded/failed `site-webhook` delivery events in demo and repository modes, and keeps custom endpoint headers isolated to that endpoint. The admin site webhook selector exposes `Site settings updated`, and `test:settings-admin-contract` source-guards the core event type, route dispatch, delivery headers/payload, timeout, and demo/repository event recording. This narrows the site-level webhook execution gap while broader provider-managed webhook certification remains external.
- **Site webhook lifecycle update**: site-level webhook configuration now also includes first-class `site-created` and `site-deleted` event kinds. `POST /api/admin/sites` dispatches enabled endpoints subscribed to `site-created` after successful demo or repository site creation, and `DELETE /api/admin/sites/:siteId` dispatches enabled endpoints subscribed to `site-deleted` with the deleted site snapshot before the record is removed. `test:site-webhook-delivery --workspace @backy/public` now exercises local HTTP delivery for create, update success/failure, and delete events, while `test:settings-admin-contract` source-guards the event type, admin selector, create/update/delete route dispatch, and shared delivery helper contract.
- **Site-scoped Settings webhook update**: `PATCH /api/admin/sites/:siteId/settings` now dispatches the same `site-updated` webhook contract after successful site-scoped Settings writes in both demo and repository modes. The payload includes before/after site settings, request id, actor, `site.settings.updated` reason, changed keys, and `admin-site-settings-api` source metadata, so integrations subscribed to site changes receive updates whether authors save through the site detail route or the dedicated site Settings route. `test:settings-admin-contract` now source-guards the site-scoped route dispatch contract.
- **Dedicated site config webhook update**: `PATCH /api/admin/sites/:siteId/seo`, `/navigation`, and `/redirects` now dispatch `site-updated` webhooks after successful site-owned SEO, navigation, and redirect changes in both demo and repository modes. Each payload carries the route-specific reason (`site.seo.updated`, `site.navigation.updated`, or `site.redirects.updated`), before/after settings data, changed-key metadata, request id, actor, and source marker so custom frontend deployment, cache, and integration workers can react consistently to every site-owned configuration write path. `test:settings-admin-contract` source-guards all three dedicated route dispatch contracts.

- **Media operations handoff/action plan**: `/media` now exports a named `backy.media-handoff.v1` manifest with `backy.media-readiness.v1`, `backy.media-operation-action-plan.v1`, and `backy.media-attribution-handoff.v1` blocks. The command center renders the same action plan for storage configuration, provisioning probes, scanner readiness, quota, attribution ingest, asset organization, and font publishing, and it now exposes a copyable attribution handoff that packages provider coverage, source/window channels, conversion/value metrics, missing evidence, and ingestion next steps for custom frontend media ROI dashboards.

The handoff lists the selected local/Supabase/S3 provider, non-secret saved metadata, required env alias names, runtime and probe evidence, provider-certification commands, missing evidence, and the explicit secret boundary so central file uploads remain tied to auditable production storage readiness without leaking credentials.
- **Media smoke auth update**: `test:media` now supports seeded admin MFA through `BACKY_MEDIA_SMOKE_MFA_CODE`, `BACKY_ADMIN_MFA_CODE`, or `BACKY_ADMIN_2FA_CODE` before driving the central media library UI/API smoke, keeping the folder/upload/font/private-file verification runnable when workspace security requires two-factor admin login.
- **Site-owned webhook coverage guard**: `test:settings-admin-contract` now scans every `apps/public/src/app/api/admin/sites/:siteId/**/route.ts` file and fails when a route records `recordSiteCacheInvalidation` without also importing `deliverSiteWebhooks`. This makes site-owned custom-frontend sync coverage enforceable across pages, blog, settings, SEO, navigation, redirects, frontend design, reusable sections, collections, media, forms, and commerce workflow mutations instead of relying on a one-off route checklist.

The generated SDK exports `GeneratedBackyOpenApiSiteWebhookPayload`, and `npm run test:generated-types --workspace @backy/sdk-js` covers both positive payloads and invalid schema-version/event-kind regressions so custom frontend and integration workers can type webhook consumers without scraping admin route internals.

- **Frontend contract taxonomy/filter update**: the frontend manifest JSON schema now generates typed blog category/tag/author summary arrays instead of `Array<unknown>`, so generated contract consumers can rely on `id`, `name`, `slug`, and `postCount` for blog archive navigation. Reusable-section category/tag filters now generate as `string[]` instead of loose arrays. - **Interactive component authoring current slice**: editor interactive blocks now select registry entries by a unique `componentKey + version` option value, then persist both the component key and pinned version into the page/blog canvas element. This prevents multiple reviewed versions of the same interactive animation or sandboxed code component from collapsing to key-only selection in the inspector. The inspector also renders runtime capability badges for status, render mode, source, signature state, sandbox route readiness, permissions, admin API access, dependency policy preset, compatibility targets, and animation-library metadata, then renders schema-driven registry controls for select, range/number, boolean/toggle, color, and text fields and persists edited values into both the element `controls` list and top-level props so trusted figures and sandbox payloads receive the configured animation state without bespoke per-component UI. Registry-declared data-binding presets now render as authoring buttons and persist the selected binding target into the canvas element, while public registry/OpenAPI/SDK contracts expose dependency policy, compatibility, and binding preset metadata for custom frontends. The inspector now also renders a compact registry-driven visual preview panel for rounds, stepper, chart, timeline, simulation, data explorer, and sandboxed canvas/custom component families, including selected title, render mode, family-specific caption, feature chips, and control-influenced miniature output. Editor publish readiness and inspector guidance now require the same Backy-owned `/api/sites/:siteId/interactive-components/:componentKey/:version/sandbox` route pattern as the server, including key/version matching, before code components can publish. Server-side registry validation rejects remote HTTPS, generic relative, wrong-key, and wrong-version custom-code sandbox URLs, requiring the Backy-owned route to match the component's resolved site, key, and version across create, update, review approval, and bundle-upload mutation paths. It also enforces dependency policy presets, blocked runtime built-ins, disabled lifecycle scripts, disabled remote runtime policies, bounded Backy runtime compatibility, render-target compatibility with the selected render mode, required static fallback compatibility, and binding preset schemas before custom-code components can advance through create/update/review/bundle mutation paths. Template breadth now includes timeline, parameter simulation, data explorer, and sandboxed canvas animation presets in the editor catalog and public registry, with admin-contract source guards for registry exposure, controls, data scopes, sandbox runtime metadata, dependency policy, compatibility metadata, binding preset pickers, and visual preview rendering. `apps/admin/scripts/editor-drag-smoke.mjs` now includes source guards for version-aware registry selection, runtime capability badges, control-value persistence, binding preset persistence, sandbox route/key/version publish gating, interactive visual preview rendering, and the broader interactive catalog, `npm run typecheck --workspace @backy-cms/admin` passes, `npm run typecheck --workspace @backy/public` passes, `npm exec --workspace @backy/public -- tsx -e "...validateInteractiveComponentPayload(...)"` accepts the owned sandbox route while rejecting remote/generic/mismatched routes and metadata render-target mismatches, and `npm run test:interactive-sandbox-security --workspace @backy/public` passes for the constrained iframe security baseline, hostile browser fixture, validator source guard, and representative animated canvas runtime fixture.
- **Interactive sandbox response hardening update**: the Backy-owned public sandbox bootstrap route now returns an explicit deny-by-default `Permissions-Policy` for camera, microphone, geolocation, payment, USB, serial, clipboard, and related browser capabilities while preserving the narrow fullscreen permission needed for selected interactive canvases. Its CSP now also denies objects, nested frames, workers, external fonts, manifests, base navigation, and form actions, with source guards in `apps/public/scripts/interactive-sandbox-security-smoke.mjs` so custom code animation support remains a governed iframe platform rather than a free-form script box.
- **Interactive runtime telemetry hardening update**: `POST /api/sites/:siteId/interactive-components/runtime-events` now normalizes runtime messages to the documented `ready`, `init`, `resize`, `error`, `fallback`, and `blocked` lifecycle set, rejects missing messages, rejects unbounded event types, and verifies the reported `componentKey`/`version` exists in the selected site's public interactive-component registry before recording an `interactive-runtime` event. The admin contract smoke includes negative coverage for invalid telemetry types and unknown component keys so public sandbox diagnostics cannot pollute the event stream with arbitrary component identities.
- **SDK interactive runtime event builder update**: `packages/sdk-js` now exports `buildBackyInteractiveRuntimeEventInput()` for generated/custom frontends that host registry-backed interactive figures or sandboxed code components. The helper normalizes sandbox `postMessage` lifecycle names, nested component/data context, and error objects into the bounded payload accepted by `recordInteractiveRuntimeEvent()`, and the runtime-event method now applies the same normalization before posting telemetry. SDK generated-type checks, SDK smoke assertions, API docs, and the SDK README guard the helper while the Frontend manifest/OpenAPI/SDK APIs row remains Partial for the disposable Supabase/Postgres SDK smoke gate.

- **Commerce/orders current slice**: `/orders` now loads non-secret Settings commerce/runtime diagnostics into a provider execution readiness panel covering Stripe checkout/refunds, tax quotes, shipping quotes, discount quotes, EasyPost/Shippo labels and tracking, HTTP/manual fulfillment dispatch, webhook settlement, and scheduled reconciliation. - **Razorpay order refund provider update**: `/orders` now has a first-class Razorpay provider-refund adapter beside Stripe, PayPal, Square, Adyen, and Mollie. `POST /api/admin/sites/:siteId/commerce/orders/:orderId/provider-refund` executes Razorpay refunds with server-only `BACKY_RAZORPAY_KEY_ID`/`BACKY_RAZORPAY_KEY_SECRET`, optional `BACKY_RAZORPAY_API_BASE_URL`, Basic auth, minor-unit amounts, Backy refund metadata, sanitized provider payload persistence, and `executionMode: "razorpay-api"`; `PATCH` refreshes refund status through `GET /v1/refunds/:id`. Settings runtime diagnostics, Settings env validation UI, Orders provider-readiness UI, Commerce provider certification selectors, release-doctor missing-credential checks, standalone/release workflows, and mock-provider CI env now include Razorpay so refund certification can target that provider without accepting unrelated payment credentials.
- **Magento catalog provider update**: `/products` now has a first-class Magento/Adobe Commerce catalog-sync adapter beside Stripe, PayPal, Paddle, Square, Shopify, BigCommerce, WooCommerce, Etsy, and HTTP. `POST /api/admin/sites/:siteId/commerce/products/:productId/provider-sync` accepts `provider=magento`, reads server-only `BACKY_MAGENTO_ACCESS_TOKEN` plus `BACKY_MAGENTO_STORE_URL` or `BACKY_MAGENTO_API_BASE_URL`, sends a Magento REST `V1/products` payload with SKU, status, stock, Backy product metadata, subscription metadata, and price, persists sanitized provider product/price metadata with `executionMode: "magento-api"`, and keeps handoff behavior when credentials are absent. Settings runtime diagnostics, Settings env validation UI, Products provider-sync controls, Commerce provider certification selectors, release-doctor missing-credential checks, standalone/release workflows, mock-provider CI env, and source guards now include Magento so catalog certification can target that provider without accepting unrelated Shopify/BigCommerce/WooCommerce/Etsy credentials.
- **Commerce provider certification workflow**: `npm run test:commerce-provider-certification-preflight-contract` now guards the manual Commerce provider certification workflow, root scripts, runtime Settings commerce diagnostics, products provider-sync controls, orders provider-readiness UI, and the existing mock-provider smoke coverage. `npm run ci:commerce-provider-certification` can run against a locally started public app or an external `BACKY_COMMERCE_CERTIFICATION_BASE_URL` and checks non-secret `runtimeCommerce` readiness for payment, tax, shipping, discount, catalog, subscription, and webhook provider groups using explicit `BACKY_COMMERCE_CERTIFY_*` flags. Required-mode failures are now scoped to the requested certification groups, so webhook-only certification does not fail on unrelated carrier credentials while shipping-only certification still fails without EasyPost/Shippo readiness. The harness now supports provider-specific certification selectors for payment, tax, shipping, discount, catalog, subscription, and provider-managed webhook groups, so CI can prove one intended provider family such as PayPal, Razorpay, TaxJar, EasyPost, Stripe promotion-code discounts, Magento, Paddle, Stripe webhooks, or Razorpay webhooks instead of accepting any unrelated credential. Local demo certification prepares only its disposable Settings commerce tax/shipping/discount provider selection, selected HTTP endpoint URLs, and webhook URL/secret reference from the explicit provider selectors or auto-detected credentials before checking readiness, while external-base certification remains read-only and verifies the provider already selected in deployed Settings where Settings selection applies so TaxJar/EasyPost/Stripe discount credentials cannot falsely certify an unrelated HTTP/manual provider and webhook certification cannot pass without an env-backed signing secret plus webhook endpoint metadata. The release doctor now also fails selected discount and webhook certification early when the env-backed endpoint/secret or selected provider credentials, including Razorpay key id/secret, are missing. The harness now also asserts that the Settings infrastructure diagnostics response includes a real commerce diagnostic group with provider checks before reporting certification readiness, preventing a false-positive provider gate if Settings stops returning commerce diagnostics, and emits non-secret `target.mode`/`externalBaseUrlConfigured` JSON evidence so release logs prove whether the run certified a local disposable instance or an external deployment. `.github/workflows/commerce-provider-certification.yml` exposes the same manual gate with real provider secrets/vars for Stripe, TaxJar, Avalara, EasyPost, Shippo, PayPal, Paddle, Square, Adyen, Mollie, Razorpay, Shopify, BigCommerce, WooCommerce, Etsy, and Magento plus HTTP discount endpoints. This creates an auditable live-provider readiness gate for products/orders while real-provider certification remains Partial until the workflow passes against configured provider accounts.

- **Backy release certification workflow**: `npm run test:release-certification-preflight-contract` now guards the manual `.github/workflows/backy-release-certification.yml` release gate, root package script wiring, audit evidence, and the `SETUP.md` runbook. - **Release certification readiness doctor**: `npm run doctor:release-certification` now emits a non-secret `backy.release-certification-doctor.v1` JSON report for database target-guard status, database URL format validity, disposable confirmation state, certification readiness, requested Settings/Commerce provider groups, local/external target mode, selected provider families, missing env variable names, and failure labels.
